Chamber of Commerce Telegraphs Ministry of Finance to Correct Customs Declaration for Civilian Ships Carrying Goods 131

The "Suzhou-Hangzhou Regulations" Refer to Tugboats

Cannot Include Ordinary Civilian Ships

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Jiaxing County Chamber of Commerce stating that the county's North-South Goods Industry, Paper Industry, Medicine and Pigment Industry, Silk and Cloth Industry, Beijing-Guangdong Goods Industry, and Eight Fresh Earth Products Industry associations reported that two cargo ships, Miao Songrong and Qia Shengxiang, traveling between Shanghai and Jiaxing, were detained by the Jianghai Customs, who demanded supplementary customs declaration procedures. This appeared to be a deliberate attempt to create difficulties. They requested assistance to advocate for their release. The Chamber of Commerce investigated and found that civilian ships transporting goods to the interior had always declared and paid taxes at the Changguan (local customs) and Goods Donation Bureau. Since the explicit order to abolish lijin (internal transit tax), all Changguan and Goods Donation Bureaus were abolished, and no clear order had been received stating that civilian ships transporting goods should declare taxes at the maritime customs. Before an explicit announcement was made, suddenly detaining ships and demanding customs declarations understandably caused merchants to protest. The Chamber of Commerce immediately sent a letter to the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office, requesting them to quickly inform the Taxation Department to release the detained ships. At the same time, twelve industry associations in Shanghai, including the Jingye, North Goods, Luzun, Bai, Guanyuan, Seafood, Domestic Pigments, Oilseed, Fruit and Earth Products, Fresh Fish, and Sesame and Sesame Oil groups, jointly sent a letter requesting their release, as there had never been such procedures before. Later, the Chamber of Commerce received a reply from the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office, forwarded by the Taxation Department, stating that it was handled according to the Suzhou-Hangzhou Regulations. The Chamber of Commerce argued that the Suzhou-Hangzhou Regulations refer to civilian ships towed by steamships carrying goods, not all civilian ships. Yesterday, it also sent a special telegram to the Ministry of Finance requesting a correction. The following are the texts of the various letters and telegrams:

Reply from Jianghai Customs: "Respected Sirs, we have received your letter No. 181 stating that the Sugar Industry and North Goods groups have sent a letter requesting the prompt release of the civilian cargo ships Miao Songrong and Qia Shengxiang, which travel between Shanghai and Jiaxing, to avoid losses. You requested us to expedite the matter and to provide a copy of any explicit order requiring civilian ships transporting goods to declare taxes at the customs. After checking with the relevant departments regarding this matter, we received a reply from the Taxation Department stating that civilian ships traveling between Shanghai and Suzhou-Hangzhou should be handled according to the long-established Suzhou-Hangzhou Regulations. The customs office has already explained this situation in detail to the representatives of the Jiaxing County Chamber of Commerce. We are replying to inform you. Please acknowledge and inform others."

Telegram to the Ministry of Finance: "Respectfully to the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, regarding the case of the Jianghai Customs detaining the two civilian ships Miao Songrong and Qia Shengxiang, this Chamber has already telegraphed and appealed on October 19th. The Shanghai Customs replied, still citing the long-established regulations for Chinese ships traveling between Suzhou, Hangzhou, and Shanghai carrying passengers and goods. Although articles 5 to 12 of these regulations contain provisions for civilian ships to declare, register, and pay taxes to the customs, according to article 1 of these regulations, these civilian ships refer to civilian ships towed by steamships carrying goods, not ordinary civilian ships. Therefore, the title of the regulations is 'Regulations for Chinese Ships Traveling between Suzhou, Hangzhou, and Shanghai Carrying Passengers and Goods.' The title of the regulations defines the scope of civilian ships. The customs offices and lijin stations each have their own jurisdiction. Civilian ships are taxed by lijin stations or Changguan, while steamships are taxed by maritime customs. This has been the practice for a long time. If the Shanghai Customs' current claim is followed, regardless of the type of civilian ship, customs duties must be declared and paid to the customs. Then, since the opening of customs in Suzhou and Hangzhou in the 21st year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, the lijin stations there would have had no taxes to collect and should have been abolished long ago, why wait until today? Now, the customs is taking advantage of the abolishment of lijin to expand its jurisdiction to civilian ships that are not towed by steamships. This has no legal basis and makes the policy of abolishing lijin a mere formality. We urgently telegraph to the Ministry for a clear explanation, ordering the customs to correct their actions, as this is in the public interest. Respectfully, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce."

Ministry of Finance Approves Tax Collection Methods for Local Indigo 134

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce received a reply from the Ministry of Finance, which stated, "We have received your submission. After investigation, the re-export tax levied by customs on local indigo sold domestically is 1 tael and 5 qian of customs silver per dan, equivalent to 2 yuan and 2 jiao and 5 fen in foreign currency. However, imported indigo is taxed at 14 gold units per dan according to the new tax rate, which is equivalent to about 28 yuan in foreign currency based on the market price. The difference between the two is significant. Moreover, the re-export tax is levied on all local goods that pass through customs, and local indigo should be treated the same. As for the Guangdong, Fujian, Jiangxi and other indigo-producing provinces' various kinds of levies, which have not been completely eliminated as mentioned in the original submission, in addition to instructing the finance departments of Guangdong, Fujian and Jiangxi to investigate and report back, it is hereby ordered that you be informed."

Dockworkers at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Wharf Demand Pay 136

Work Slowdown Occurs

Mediation and Reconciliation

Yesterday, the dockworkers and other employees of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company engaged in a work slowdown because they were owed wages. They sent representatives to the company to demand payment, while also engaging in a work slowdown. Subsequently, the heads of various departments intervened to mediate and promised to raise funds for payment. The situation was temporarily resolved. The details are as follows:

Dockworkers Demand Pay at Five Wharves: The employees and workers at the five wharves of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, including Jin Liyuan, Yangjiadu, Zhongzhan, Beizhan, and Huazhan, and the staff in the warehouses, have not yet received their salaries for September. Yesterday afternoon, the five wharves jointly elected more than thirty employee representatives to go to the headquarters to demand payment from the accounting department. At the same time, all five wharves uniformly engaged in a work slowdown and would not resume work until they received their salaries. The section chief of the general affairs department came forward to meet them. The employee representatives stated that the employees' lives were difficult and unsustainable. If they were not paid, they would have no choice but to strike completely and sit at the company to demand payment. The section chief of the general affairs department accepted the representatives' request but explained that since the government sent personnel to thoroughly investigate the accounts, the banks were hesitant to pay out any funds. Even the company's employees have not been paid. This was not discrimination against the wharves. He hoped that the representatives would persuade the wharf workers not to continue the work slowdown. He promised that they would definitely raise funds to pay the September salaries by the end of this month. The representatives demanded that the section chief take responsibility before returning to their wharves. If the salaries were not paid by the end of the month, the five wharves would strike together. The matter was resolved at 5:30 PM, and they will resume normal work today.

Negotiations by Ship Crew: The company's ocean liners Jiahe and Gongping, etc., arrived in Shanghai from the north and south. The shipping department assigned the two ships to depart immediately for foreign ports. The officers, firefighters, and sailors demanded their wages from the company. Since the ships were leaving port, everyone needed to provide for their families first. They had been owed wages for two months, and did not know how they could live. The crews of both ships went to the company to demand payment from the accounting department. The accounting department had no funds to pay. The Jiahe and Gongping immediately engaged in a work slowdown, stopping the acceptance of passengers and goods, and sat at the company to demand payment. They said that the crew members had risked their lives at sea to produce for the company, but their wages had been owed for a long time. Unless they received their wages, they would not start work. The situation almost broke down. Later, the head of the shipping department stepped in to mediate, saying that the ships that were leaving port should be paid first so that the crew members could provide for their families. He urged them to resume work while negotiating with the accounting department to pay the salaries of the Gongping, Jiahe, and other ships as soon as possible, to avoid work slowdowns, delays, and disruption to transportation. The matter was resolved late in the evening.

Judgement on Yuan An and Zhong Wei's Ship Charter Termination 138

The Sino-Japanese Incident Has Indeed Constituted War

Yuan An Wins Lawsuit; Zhong Wei Must Return All Payments

The Yuan An Steamship Company and the Shanghai Zhong Wei Steamship Company, due to the termination of a ship charter agreement, raised the question of whether the January 28th Japanese attack on Shanghai constituted a formal war. The Yuan An Company had signed a long-term ship charter agreement with Zhong Wei Company on December 5th of last year, whereby Zhong Wei leased the "Taiping" steamship, with a deadweight of 3,500 tons, to Yuan An for cargo transport at a monthly rental of 13,500 yuan, payable in advance monthly. The agreement stipulated that if war broke out between China and any country, affecting the agreement in any way, either party could terminate it. However, only two days after Yuan An prepaid the second installment of rent, the January 28th Incident suddenly occurred. Therefore, on February 3rd, based on the terms of the agreement, Yuan An notified Zhong Wei of the contract termination. At that time, the "Taiping" steamship was in Tanggu transporting cargo, and Yuan An specifically telegraphed the captain to remain under Zhong Wei's command. However, Zhong Wei Company completely disagreed with Yuan An's claims. They argued that although there were hostile acts between China and Japan, no formal declaration of war had been made, so it could not constitute a war between nations in a legal sense. Therefore, they refused to terminate the contract and would not refund the prepaid payments to Yuan An. Yuan An's manager, Zhao Yunsheng, hired lawyers Yang Linzhi, Zhang Jiajia, and Ye Shaoying to file a lawsuit with the First Special District Court against Chen Shuntong, the manager of Zhong Wei, seeking termination of the charter agreement and requesting a judgement ordering the defendant to return 14,150.81 yuan. At the trial, the plaintiff's lawyers, based on Chinese and foreign legal principles and the various brutal acts of the Japanese army during wartime, argued that even without a declaration of war, war had indeed been constituted. They presented all evidence to prove the payments made. The defendant hired lawyers Wei Wenhan and Lu Jianai to defend, stating that since September 18th of last year, although there had been continuous resistance in various places in China, it could not be considered war. This was evidenced by the declarations of China's diplomatic authorities and China's representatives to the League of Nations. Therefore, the plaintiff could not use the terms of the agreement as an excuse for termination. Moreover, when the January 28th Incident occurred, the "Taiping" steamship was in Tianjin, preparing to sail to Guangdong, which was far from the Shanghai conflict and did not pose an obstruction. Even regarding the Shanghai port, Chinese ships entered and exited daily during the intense fighting. Therefore, the plaintiff could not invoke Article 41 of the agreement as a basis for termination. Furthermore, the plaintiff's prepaid rent and other items according to the agreement could not be claimed for return under general legal principles. They requested that the original lawsuit be dismissed. Judge Yang delivered a judgement, recognizing that the incident had indeed constituted what is called war and that the plaintiff's request for termination was entirely justified. Therefore, the termination was granted. This judgement not only resolves the dispute in this case but also provides assistance for future negotiations with Japan. The reasons stated in the judgement are excerpted as follows:

The key points of the investigation in this case are (1) whether the plaintiff's termination complies with the terms agreed upon by both parties, and (2) whether the request for the return of prepaid freight and other items can be legally recognized as justified. Regarding the first point, the termination conditions in the original agreement are two: (A) war, and (B) the agreement being affected by the war. Based on this investigation, the so-called "war," according to the true intentions of the parties when signing the contract, does not specifically refer to a war automatically and universally waged by China against any country. Moreover, regarding the definition of war, it is when there is a dispute between one country or two or more countries, and the dispute includes various violent acts, then it has constituted what is called war. As for whether the general effects of war are present, it is not of great importance. Therefore, the plaintiff's argument for termination based on the January 28th Shanghai war is not inappropriate. Furthermore, according to the conditions stipulated in the original agreement that the agreement is affected by the war, one cannot argue that the condition for termination has not been fulfilled solely because Shanghai or other ports can still navigate during the Shanghai war, meaning the agreement has not been affected or obstructed. This is because the objective development of the war at that time could not be predicted by the parties, and the situation of coastal cargo transport is difficult to infer based on normal conditions. The plaintiff's agent stated that the Shanghai war had affected the agreement, which is difficult to consider unreasonable. Therefore, the plaintiff's request for termination is entirely justified. Regarding the second point, according to Article 77 of the Maritime Law, if the shipper terminates a voyage contract established for continuous navigation, the shipper should pay the full freight, and the freight already prepaid cannot be requested for return, which goes without saying. In this case, both parties entered into a time charter agreement for continuous navigation, in other words, a charter agreement for a predetermined period of transportation, which is fundamentally different from voyage transportation under Articles 75 and 76 of the Maritime Law. According to the above explanation, regarding the prepaid freight, the plaintiff can only deduct it based on Article 96 of the Maritime Law, three-quarters of the freight earned from other loaded cargo, and all expenses saved due to the termination. There is no possibility of requesting the remaining prepaid freight to be returned. If it were not so, when a ship is far from its home port and does not obtain sufficient cargo, the shipowner would inevitably suffer significant losses. However, the ship security deposit and fumigation fees, along with prepaid coal, totaling 3,800.81 yuan, are not within the scope of freight. Therefore, the defendant should return the full amount. Based on Article 82 of the Civil Procedure Law, the judgement is specially made as stated in the main text.

Assassination Case in Yangjiazhai, Pudong, Yesterday Afternoon 139

The Deceased Was "Sanbao" of the Wharf

In Charge of Insurance for Merchant Steamships

The Assailant Fired as Many as Five Shots

The Truth Behind the Attack Is Unclear

"Sanbao" (nickname) of the wharf, who was the head of insurance for various merchant steamships of the North and South Seas lines of the China Merchants Bureau, had considerable influence in the area from the Sixteenth Wharf to Xinkaihe. Unexpectedly, at noon yesterday, as he walked out of his home in Pudong and reached Tudi Tang Street, he was suddenly assassinated by an enemy with gunfire, shot twice and killed. The event caused a stir in the surrounding area, and onlookers crowded the scene. The details of the assassination obtained from the investigation are recorded below:

Assailant Pursued and Shot; The deceased, named Ye Sanbao, lived at No. 3, Lane 78, Yangjiazhai Road, Pudong. Yesterday, at 12:15 PM, after lunch at home, he put on a regular green woolen short overcoat and intended to go to Puxi. As he walked north on Yangjiazhai Road and turned west onto Tudi Tang Street, a slender man wearing a felt hat, who had been lying in wait there, saw Ye approaching and suddenly pulled out a pistol and fired three shots in a row, none of which hit him. However, one bullet entered the Xinchunji Barber Shop at that location, shattering a piece of glass, fortunately without injuring anyone. Ye, now in a state of panic, ran wildly and immediately took refuge in the Dongwanmao Oil Shop at No. 73 on that street. By this time, the enemy had already chased him to the shop entrance and fired two more shots at Ye, one bullet hitting the right breast and the other lodging in the right rib cage, neither of which penetrated. Ye, wounded, lost his footing and fell backwards outside the counter in the shop, head inside and feet outside, covered in blood. The assailant, seeing that his goal had been achieved, fled west, turning south into Lane 69 and disappearing. The family members, hearing the alarm, rushed to the scene, but Ye was already staring blankly with his mouth closed, though still barely breathing. He soon died of his injuries.

Police from the Third District Investigate; Upon learning of the incident, the Third District Police immediately dispatched officers to pursue the assailant, but he was nowhere to be found. Since there were too many onlookers at the scene of the incident, Inspector Liu Huansheng led police officers to maintain order. The Dongwanmao Oil Shop was also closed and temporarily ceased business. Subsequently, District Chief Zhang personally arrived at the scene to inspect and question nearby residents about the circumstances of the shooting. He then ordered that the body be temporarily left in place pending an autopsy, and instructed the local bailiff Xie Along to submit a request to the local court for an autopsy. It is said that due to timing issues, personnel will be dispatched across the river tomorrow morning for an autopsy, so Sanbao's body remains in place overnight.

Investigation of the Deceased's Background; It is learned that Ye was 35 years old, from northern Zhejiang. Seven or eight years ago, he became acquainted with a local widow named Ma, and they lived together at No. 3, Lane 78, Yangjiazhai Road, Pudong. Ma already had a son named Liudao, around 20 years old, who worked as a coppersmith in the XiangSheng Iron Factory. He was not yet married, so they lived together in the same household. After Ma became acquainted with Sanbao, she gave birth to another son named Fudao, who is now four years old. Ye is currently the head of insurance for the North and South Seas lines of merchant steamships Xinming, Xinfeng, Gongping, Yushun, Jiahe, and Tunan of the Jinliyuan Wharf under the China Merchants Bureau, employing many insurance agents. When each ship arrives at the port, they are responsible for protecting the goods being loaded and unloaded. If there is any theft, Ye is responsible, so his income is quite good.

Speculation on the Reasons for the Murder; Ye had considerable influence in the wharf area and was known as "Sanbao of the Wharf." Ye also bought the leftover, unusable paper scraps from the Nanyang Tobacco Factory and resold them to paper mills, making a considerable profit. Therefore, in recent years, his family has become quite wealthy, unlike the previous days when he was dissolute and unemployed. As for the reason for this sudden assassination, according to various speculations by onlookers, it may be that Ye had made enemies with people due to various matters, leading to this attack, or it may be related to a love triangle. Rumors are rampant, and it is impossible to determine the truth.

Two of the Nine Kidnapped Men and Women Escape Home 140

Terrible Condition Upon Returning Home, Covered in Sacks

Hands and Feet Bound with Wire, Suffering Unspeakable Pain

Li Jisheng (nickname "Old Foreigner"), a villager from the coastal area about two li north of Chuansha in Baoshan County, became wealthy after rescuing a Westerner at sea. When Li Jisheng passed away, he left hundreds of acres of land in the western countryside. His eldest son, Li Fengming (known as "Little Foreigner"), and other men and women, a total of nine people, were kidnapped by bandits in September and held for a ransom of 300,000 yuan. Details of this were reported in this newspaper on September 27th. Now, it is learned that Liu and Wang, two of the five women among those kidnapped, suddenly escaped from the bandits' den yesterday and returned home safely. However, when the two women escaped, they were in a terrible condition, not only haggard but also completely without clothes, covered only in sacks. Their tragic state is difficult to describe. The cruelty of the bandits is shocking and appalling. According to Liu and others, after they were kidnapped, they were hidden in a dilapidated house in Dasha, across from Liuh River. The nine men and women were hidden in two separate places. Liu and the other four women were held in the same house. During the day, they were not given enough to eat and were often beaten, leaving them covered in injuries. They were forced to pay a ransom, but when they replied that they were imprisoned and had no money for a ransom, the bandits were unreasonable. At night, their clothes were stripped off, and their hands and feet were bound with wire, causing unspeakable pain. Fortunately, a bamboo craftsman nearby, who knew the bandit guard, took pity on our suffering and secretly hid a pair of scissors. That evening, taking advantage of the bandits' inattention, he cut the wires on our hands and feet. He went back first, and late at night, the two of us escaped first, and the other three women followed. Before long, the bandits discovered our escape and searched in all directions. The bandits caught the three women behind us, but we two were fortunate enough to escape into the home of a villager, who kindly allowed us to stay until dawn and gave us clothes to wear before we were able to escape home. As she spoke, tears streamed down her face, undoubtedly due to the suffering she experienced in the bandits' den.

Due to two incidents of freight train robbery occurring on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway in Huangdu and Zhenru, Jian Huanluan, the police chief of Maigen Road, has assumed heavy responsibility for the implementation of freight train transportation and is diligently investigating the matter. It is now learned that the leaders of the notorious freight train robbers, Wang Dahanzi (also known as Wu Licai), Li Baoshun (also known as Li Mapi, wanted by the patrol station), Jia Laosi, and Xu Xiaobianzi, possess extraordinary skills and can jump onto moving trains at high speed to steal goods, earning them the nickname "Four King Kongs." They initially committed robberies on trains in the north and have been rampant for years, with hundreds of accomplices. The Shanghai-Nanjing Railway has repeatedly suffered from organized freight train robberies, but none have been solved. Recently, such as the robbery of four freight trains on August 25th in the Huangdu area and the robbery of train No. 465 near Zhenru on September 28th, where they fired shots as a warning, were all committed by these four notorious robbers. The Railway Bureau, which is currently responsible for transportation, urgently needs to eliminate them to maintain freight transport. It has issued orders to the police stations to conduct strict arrests. Currently, Jian Huanluan, the police chief of Maigen Road, has secretly offered a large reward and set up informants to investigate the whereabouts of the notorious robbers Wang Dahanzi and others, who are hiding near Zhenru. Commissioner Ma, considering police chief Jian's expertise in investigation, again dispatched him and police sergeant Li Demao to the capital to obtain informants and confirm his location. They cooperated with the police department of the capital and arrested the robber Jia Laosi in Pukou and brought him back to Shanghai. Subsequently, the bandit confessed that in 1928, he was arrested for robbing a train in Kunshan and sentenced to four years in prison. He was released in June of this year, and in August, he colluded with Wang, Li, and others to rob a train. Some of his accomplices, Xu Fengshan and Shen Jinfu, were arrested by the Hongkou patrol station more than ten days ago. Commissioner Ma Shaoping and Deputy Commissioner Li Dingrong reviewed the case and determined that the bandits had been rampant on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway for years, openly robbing and committing numerous crimes, which were not comparable to ordinary cases. Strict punishment was necessary to maintain public order. They ordered police chief Jian to send the three bandits, Wang, Li, and Jia, to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters on the 26th of this month and requested military justice.

Two Guilds of Cured Meat and Ham Businesses to Petition Party and Government Authorities Today 151

Requesting Complete Cancellation of Inspection Measures

Stating Four Reasons: No Inferior Products

The two guilds of cured meat and ham businesses in this city have scheduled to dispatch sixteen representatives to the city's Party headquarters, the municipal government, and the municipal chamber of commerce this morning to petition for the cancellation of inspection issues. The recorded petition is as follows: A petition for the cancellation of the city's inspection of cured meats and hams, hoping for fair consideration. We, the guilds, received a joint official letter from the city's Health and Finance Bureaus in July of this year, relayed by the municipal chamber of commerce, stating that hams and cured meats were planned for import inspection, and that a fee of half a dollar per hundred catties would be charged for inspection. Subsequently, the guilds repeatedly sent representatives to negotiate with the municipal chamber of commerce, stating that if this inspection fee was collected, the industry would find it difficult to agree. After the cured meat industry first submitted a written statement of opposition, the municipal chamber of commerce then forwarded a reply from the Finance and Health Bureaus. Whether ham and cured meat are detrimental to health and whether inspection is necessary are matters that the industry urgently wants to clarify, sparing no effort. We now respectfully present the factual situation of the industry as follows: (1) Ham and cured meat are invariably made during the winter season when the weather is cold, so where do diseased animal meats come from? Therefore, in Chinese custom, when people are ill, they avoid eating various vegetables, but ham and cured meat can be used as a condiment. This is because ham and cured meat have undergone legitimate production supervision and are not harmful to health, thus eliminating the need for inspection. (2) Merchants invest in business to seek profit, and can diseased animal meat be made into cured meat? Anyone with a clear understanding of the matter will surely say no. As for the careful selection during the production of ham, it goes without saying. Although diseased animal meat is difficult to avoid for livestock farmers, cured meat and ham businesses invest in meat, produce products, and even the most foolish people would not buy inferior meat and manufacture inferior products, thus ruining their capital. Therefore, in theory, there is no possibility of unhealthy, inferior meat being mixed into ham and cured meat, thus eliminating the need for inspection. (3) Our country has been established for over five thousand years. Although there is no definite historical record of the method of making ham and cured meat, in the areas of Jinhua, where it is produced, people slaughter fat pigs during the winter to make ham and cured meat for future needs. Because of its delicious taste and long shelf life, it was gradually sold to other areas. Later, there were many who enjoyed eating it, and areas north of the Yangtze River, such as Gaoyou and Taixing, also became production areas for ham and cured meat. Shandong's La pigs also followed suit. Looking at the current merchants in the Jiangbei area who produce ham, most of them are from Jinhua, which shows that ham and cured meat are the most economical food for the people. There are no reports of people dying from poisoning from eating ham and cured meat, let alone diseased animal meat being mixed in, thus eliminating the need for inspection. (4) According to the reply from the city's Finance and Health Bureaus, the inspection is being carried out to protect the health of the two million meat-eating people in Shanghai. If this inspection is truly as stated, then the production areas of ham and cured meat, such as Jinhua, Jiangbei, and Shandong, are all part of our country's territory. Why not issue a unified order to carry out pre- and post-slaughter inspections? Now, if only the market where it is sold is inspected, it is putting the cart before the horse, which is not only not beneficial in fact, but also unfair in principle, thus eliminating the need for inspection. Based on the above four reasons, we are only addressing the most salient points. Commercial difficulties, economic hardship, and overlapping taxes have made it difficult for merchants and the people to bear. Moreover, since the Japanese invaded Shanghai and the war broke out, the market has been extremely depressed, making it unbearable to add harsh policies and burden the people. Considering the past and looking to the future, the guilds are heartbroken and witness this situation. Therefore, we have no choice but to send representatives Yang Chenhu, Wang Tingsheng, Cai Xiaozhi, Zhang Dongyun, Xue Chunrong, Kong Guangyuan, Qian Yibiao, Chen Rongsheng, Wang Mingdeng, Lu Degao, Dai Songfu, Pan Jinluo, Xu Yinshu, Zhang Ji'an, Cao Yongzhang, Xi Danru, and sixteen others to petition, earnestly requesting that the authorities (chamber of commerce) review and approve the cancellation of the ham and cured meat inspection measures by the Health and Finance Bureaus in order to alleviate the hardships of merchants, which would be a public service. (The following is omitted)

Alcohol Dispute Completely Resolved Yesterday 152

Settled in a Reconciliation Record Signed at the Social Bureau

The alcohol workshops in Pudong, including Xinji and Wanyuan in Hujia Muqiao, and Fuji in Lujiadu, had a labor dispute caused by the employers dismissing a large number of workers without reason. The dispute has been going on for a long time and has not been resolved. Yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m., a formal mediation was held again at the Social Bureau. Those present included Tan Peiyan, the mediator from the Social Bureau, Li Weixiong, the representative from the City Party Headquarters, Wang Bingkui and Lin Xiaofang, the representatives from the labor union, Fang Zhongheng and Zhu Qingtang, the representatives from the employer's association. Chairman Tan Peiyan started by having the labor representative report on the dispute's history, followed by debate. Finally, with the chairman's repeated guidance to both sides, a settlement was reached. Then both parties signed a reconciliation record, the contents of which are as follows: (1) The industry association will persuade Xinji workers Lin Xiaofang and Tang Zhixian, Fuji worker Shen Guomin, and Wanyuan worker Yu Shuiqiao to continue to be employed by the alcohol workshops. (2) Xinji workers Lin Zhilin and Shen A'er, and Fuji worker Chen Yaohan, who are in Shanghai, will each be given 15 yuan for travel expenses to return home. Workers not in Shanghai are not included in this clause.

Municipality Orders Restraint on Husi Weighing Practices 153

Heavier Measures Added to Scales

The Municipal Government and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and Rice Industry Association yesterday received a telegram from the Jiashan County Rice Industry Association stating that Shanghai husi (rice shops) often use heavier measures and add weight to the scales, with rice buyers losing three liters per shi (unit of dry measure) in undisclosed wastage. The rice shops do not stop this practice, leading to repeated disputes. The Jiashan County Rice Industry Association urges that fair restraint be ordered to show impartiality, and that rice boat owners be advised to continue business as usual to avoid huge losses. Considering the people's food supply, the association urgently sends a telegram to plead for action. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has forwarded the letter to the rice industry organization for verification and handling.

Yang Shengzhi's Concubines' Property Dispute Lawsuit 155

Wang Jiazhen Surrendered to Await Interrogation

Postponed Due to Cai Huaxian's Absence

The two concubines of the late Army 10th Division Commander Yang Shengzhi, Wang Jiazhen and Cai Huaxian, are involved in a lawsuit in the First Special District Court over the 120,000 yuan deposited in the Bank of China and the Central South Bank during Commander Yang's lifetime. Wang had requested that the funds be seized first, but Cai colluded with Sun Luan, the manager of the China Industrial Bank, to withdraw the funds in advance, rendering the court's seizure order ineffective. Wang Jiazhen then filed a criminal self-accusation against Cai Huaxian, Sun Luan, and Yang Xiuqian, Cai's son, accusing them of conspiring to conceal assets and obstructing enforcement, requesting a swift investigation. This has already been reported in the newspapers. Yesterday afternoon at 2:30 p.m., the case was scheduled for public hearing. Wang Jiazhen, accompanied by her lawyer, reported to the Fourth Court of the First Special District Court as scheduled. The woman was young, fair-skinned, slender, fashionable, with a bobbed haircut, leather shoes, wearing a black lined cheongsam, and a beige vest, standing tall and elegant, further enhancing her beauty. However, none of the three defendants appeared, only their lawyer. The lawyer stated that the defendants Cai Huaxian and Yang Xiuqian, mother and son, both lived in Nanjing and were unable to surrender themselves today, requesting a postponement. However, according to the plaintiff's lawyer, Cai and her son were actually in Shanghai, and Sun Luan was also believed to be in Shanghai. If Sun had been transferred to Tianjin by the bank, the Tianjin court should be consulted for assistance. However, the plaintiff also heard that the defendant Cai Huaxian was eager to withdraw the deposit and transport Commander Yang's coffin back to her ancestral home in Guizhou. If further delays allowed the defendant to realize this plan, the plaintiff would be further affected. The defendant's lawyer stated that the defendants resided in Nanjing, and Yang Xiuqian was only twelve years old. Judge Huang stated that as the defendants had not appeared, it was difficult to proceed with the trial, and instructed the defendant's lawyer to notify the defendants to come to Shanghai as soon as possible to await scheduling for interrogation. The lawyer complied, and the court adjourned.

Tenants of Yongxiang Lane in Zhabei Request Rent Reduction 158

Petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday

Since the withdrawal of Japanese troops from Zhabei, the market conditions are no longer as prosperous as before. The tenants of Yongxiang Lane on Datong Road claim that the rents set in the lane, 28 yuan per month for each two-story shikumen house in the lane, and 40-50 yuan per room in the market building, are much higher than those in nearby lanes. Furthermore, during the Municipal Government's restoration of Zhabei, such high rents should not be imposed. In order to alleviate the unbearable burden, the tenants of the lane requested the landlord, Shunxiang Real Estate Company, to voluntarily reduce the rent. Due to the landlord's strong attitude, they petitioned the Party and government authorities for relief. Yesterday, they publicly elected representatives Xie Baoxing and more than ten others to petition the municipal government, which received them. It was said that the petition has been submitted to the Rent Dispute Committee for deliberation, and a fair resolution is expected soon.

Bandits From Changzhou Approved for Transfer 160

On August 22nd of this year, several bandits suddenly came to the home of Song Liu, a resident of Dong Tangjia Village, Jinniu Township, Wujin County, Changzhou, and abducted her two-year-old son Fang Rong. Afterwards, they sent a letter to Song, demanding a ransom of 3,000 yuan. Song reported the matter to the local authorities, requesting an investigation. Later, Song received repeated letters from the bandits, and the ransom was reduced from 3,000 yuan to 1,500 yuan, ordering them to contact them at the Qunle Tea House at No. 704 Maigen Road in Shanghai. Song Liu then sent Wang Baocheng as a representative to Shanghai. After meeting the bandit Zhang Zilong (also known as Hongsheng), they negotiated a ransom of 300 yuan and agreed to hand over the money at 5 p.m. the day before yesterday. Wang reported this to Song Liu, who reported it to the Wujin County Public Security Bureau. Detective Ni Gusheng and Wu Hanwen, the Wujin resident detective in Shanghai, came to Shanghai by car the day before yesterday. After reporting to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, they met with Liu Chunshu, the Chinese detective of the Gordon Road Police Station, and secretly went to the Qunle Tea House to wait. At around 5 p.m., Zhang and his accomplice Shen Jinfu (also known as Ma Zi Ne Gen) arrived. The detectives immediately arrested Zhang and Shen and took them into custody at the police station. Yesterday morning, Gao Wansheng, a detective from the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, surrendered to the First Special District Court, requesting approval for transfer in order to bring the case to justice. The victim Song Liu also testified: I am a resident of Changzhou, 30 years old. On July 21st, Zhang Hongsheng and others came to my home and took my son Fang Rong, then sent me a letter demanding a ransom. Therefore, I sent Wang Baocheng to Shanghai to negotiate. I don't know anything else. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau requested the transfer of the case, and the police did not object. However, since they did not bring official documents today, they should be ordered to submit them, and the defendants should be taken away first. After Judge Ge Ci questioned Zhang and Shen, he approved their handover to Gao Wansheng, an officer from the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, to be taken away and brought to justice.

At 7 p.m. last night, eight bandits suddenly came to the home of Huang Yunzhi at No. 6 Henglu Road, Xiangyan Bridge, Zhabei. All were wearing blue cloth shirts and pants, spoke with a Jiangbei accent, and only two bandits carried guns. Electricity Restoration Imminent in Wusong 162

The Baoming Electric Plant in Wusong suffered losses due to the war and was unable to resume operations. After a resolution by the shareholders of the plant, it was merged into the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company. However, due to unsettled terms, the merger has been delayed until now, causing the restoration of light in the entire town of Wusong to be indefinite. The municipal public security authorities have also repeatedly requested the municipal government to order the plant to resume operations as soon as possible. It is now learned that the plant has reached an agreement with the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to formally merge, and the Yongdian Company has appointed Shen Kuibai as the director of the Wusong office (the former Baoming plant site). Yesterday, a large number of workers were hired to rush the work of erecting poles and laying lines throughout the town. When the reporter met with Director Shen and inquired about the date of power restoration, he said that electricity could be generated and light restored after the lines throughout the town of Wusong were completed. As for Paotaiwan and Baoshan, it is also planned to gradually restore them after the preliminary work is completed.

Penalties for Failure to Affix Stamps to Invoices and Account Books 163

Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court opened a trial for cases of violating the Stamp Tax Regulations. Twelve defendants, except for Taikang Western Clothing Store, whose address did not match and could not be summoned, the other eleven were summoned to court for failing to affix stamps to invoices and receipts. After a brief interrogation by Judge Shen Shanzeng, they all confessed to the omission. The court then sentenced Yongdaxiang Sesame Oil Shop to a fine of 140 yuan, Hengtai Rice Shop to a fine of 90 yuan, Shenzhou Hotel to a fine of 40 yuan, Lao Yan Maoyuan Shaoxing Liquor Shop to a fine of 20 yuan, and Shengchang Yellow Sand Shop, Yuantai Iron Shop, Chengyuanji Soda Shop, China Chemical Industry, Dafu Southern Goods Shop, Dajiali Western Restaurant, and Sanxing Water and Electricity Company to fines of 12 yuan each. Furthermore, the account books of Yuanxiang Silk and Cloth Shop in Qujiang Lane, Sanma Road, had not been affixed with stamps. After being reported, the Shanghai Special Zone Stamp Tax Office sent personnel, together with judicial police and Chinese and Western detectives from the police station, carrying court search warrants, to the shop and seized twenty-two account books that had not been affixed with stamps or had insufficient stamps. These were handed over to the police station for handling. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court also opened a joint trial. Judge Xu imposed a fine of 10 to 100 yuan per item for not affixing stamps according to the Stamp Tax Regulations, and sentenced the shop to a fine of 280 yuan. The account books were returned to the shop in court.

Three Homicide Cases Investigated 170

Quan Suo'er, a Tongzhou native residing in the Linjiazhai area of Yangjing, Pudong, was very poor and worked as a dockworker. He married a woman named Zhang, who was 18 years old. She was usually able to work and help out, but due to the high cost of living, any illness would lead to starvation. Recently, Zhang fell ill and was unable to work, which made her feel that life was meaningless. She hanged herself in bed. Her husband returned home and was unable to save her. He reported the incident to the Second Precinct of the Third District, and the local bailiff reported it to the local court for investigation.

Zhou Qiaoyuan's six-year-old son, Zhou Xiyuan, from Jiading, was playing in front of his door on the west side of Zhongxing Road and Gonghexin Road yesterday morning when he was hit by a speeding truck, which crushed his head and killed him instantly. Letter to the Editor 174

To the Esteemed Editor,

Your newspaper recently reported that Ding Fubao, who was arrested by the police for privately possessing firearms, morphine, and red pills, has been extradited, etc. I am Ding Fubao, the compiler of Shuowen Gu Lin and the Buddhist Dictionary, and my name is exactly the same. Sincerely,

Ding Fubao, Doctor

204 Meibaige Road, Shanghai

Special Delivery

Judge Feetham's Report on Conditions in the Shanghai International Settlement, Volume IV (5) 175

1. Number of Standing Committees

32. The number of Standing Committees should be limited. I believe that there should be no more than five or six. All work supervising the various departments of the Municipal Council should be undertaken separately by these five or six Standing Committees. If the various committees meet on a regular basis, then the proposed number limitation is truly appropriate. If there is no limitation, then the amount of time spent by the directors to attend various committee meetings will inevitably be excessive. I know that there are currently ten committees, including the Education Committee, the Library Committee, and the Band Committee. These two committees are different from the other committees because the number of events submitted for review and handling is limited, and the number of members is also small. They can be called special committees to distinguish them from standing committees. The number of times the two committees meet probably does not need to be as frequent as the proposed standing committee meeting times. I believe that the work of the various committees can be redistributed, and five or at most six standing committees, including the Education Committee, can be used to replace the remaining eight committees, without hindering the duties of the Municipal Council.

2. Scope of Authority of the Committees

33. The authority of the Standing Committees should be defined in such a way that the authority and responsibilities of each committee have clear limits, and that there is a clear distinction between the executive and advisory tasks of the committees. This means that the committees may handle certain matters in accordance with their authority, while for other matters, they must submit their recommendations to the Board of Directors for consideration. I have now included in the appendix certain documents regarding the committee system implemented in Johannesburg (Note 15). This document is sufficient to explain some of the suggestions made regarding committees and provide examples, including the style of the articles of association used by all standing committees of the Johannesburg City Council. According to the provisions of this article of association, the Standing Committees have the right to manage specific departments separately. The appointment and removal of all other staff members other than the heads of the departments is considered by the responsible Standing Committee and a report is prepared. The appointment and removal of the heads of the departments is left to the General Affairs Committee. The Selection Committee of the Public Concession Municipal Council, as defined by its scope of authority, (examines general issues regarding the salaries and service regulations of staff members). According to the established practice in the bureau, the issue of the appointment of personnel in various departments should first be submitted to the Selection Committee for consideration. I assume that the original purpose of adopting this method was mostly to unify the service conditions of the various departments of the Municipal Council. Now that a clear grading system has been adopted as a result of the establishment of the Salary Committee, encompassing all positions in the Municipal Council, the current organization of the Selection Committee may no longer be necessary. I believe that the appointment and promotion of staff members in each department should be the responsibility of the Standing Committee that has a special relationship with that department, and that the recommendations should be made to the Board of Directors, or that they should be promoted separately in accordance with the powers granted by the Board of Directors. For example, the appointment and removal of staff members of the Works Department is the responsibility of the Works Committee, the appointment and removal of staff members of the Health Department is the responsibility of the Health Committee, and so on.

Regarding the powers and responsibilities of the Finance Committee, I intend to present them in another chapter, so I will not discuss the various issues that have a special relationship with that committee here.

3. Meetings of the Standing Committees

34. Meetings of the Standing Committees should be held every few days, within the range of possibility. That is, except in any necessary exceptional circumstances, a regular meeting should be held once every two weeks between two consecutive regular meetings of the Board of Directors, so that a report from each committee can be submitted for consideration each time a regular meeting of the Board of Directors is held.

35. The more frequent the committee meetings and the more executive power the Standing Committees are subject to, the more the opportunity to use the method of circulating documents for discussion can be greatly limited. A certain clause in the rules of the Board of Directors stipulates that any event that is circulated in a document but does not receive unanimous approval should be listed on the agenda of the next meeting. In addition to the fact that the directors must study the circulated documents and other items as part of their responsibilities, and that it may be inconvenient to circulate them due to busy schedules, this system is still objectionable. There is no opportunity for discussion when consulting by circulating documents, and if the event being consulted is submitted to a meeting of the Board of Directors or a meeting of the committee, one or two directors may raise some questions or arguments, but because this business has been approved by other directors, or because they are unwilling to ask to postpone the discussion and wait for a later discussion, this matter is delayed in decision.

4. Reports of the Committees

36. The minutes of the committee meetings and the committee reports submitted to the Board of Directors should be different. If a committee report system is adopted, the contents of the committee meeting minutes can be shortened, so that they include no more than the written reports of the bureau members obtained by the committee and the resolutions of the committee. The preparation of the committee report (Note 16) should enable the Board of Directors to clearly understand the various major events raised at the committee meeting. The various parts of each event should be marked with sequential numbers to facilitate reference. Some parts of the report only need to be presented to the Board of Directors, such as reports on the progress and statistics of the work of the departments in charge of the committee, and the committee's resolutions on matters that can be finally disposed of in accordance with its authority. However, for all matters that need to be decided by the Board of Directors, the report should clearly state all relevant facts, summarize the various arguments that have been considered by the committee and the reasons on which its conclusions are based, and make a recommendation to the Board of Directors to indicate how to proceed. This report, although signed by the chairman of the committee or another member who served as chairman at the meeting, should usually be drafted by the secretary of the committee under the supervision of the chief administrator of the Municipal Council. Most of this report should be based on the reports submitted to the committee by the heads of the relevant departments. The reports of the department heads can often be quoted verbatim, but it must also indicate all the major debates that took place during the committee's meeting, or the arguments that were raised, which are usually included in the committee's meeting minutes according to current practice. The benefits of submitting the committee's affairs to the Board of Directors in the form of a report are far greater than presenting them in the form of meeting minutes, because the content of the report can be arranged in such a way that all the issues are clearly expressed, and the various arguments are narrated according to their natural order. As for the meeting minutes, they are fundamentally only a record of the discussion process, and all the arguments in them are often presented in a mixed-up manner.

5. Procedure for Reviewing Committee Reports at Board of Directors Meetings

37. The following procedure (Note 17) should be adopted at Board of Directors meetings to dispose of the committee's reports, that is, the report is submitted by the chairman of the committee, but a copy should be sent to each director before the meeting. If each director can have a copy of this report before disposing of the committee's report at the Board of Directors meeting, it will be much easier to dispose of it. When the chairman of the committee submits the report, he should move that the Board of Directors accept the report. Although, generally speaking, this motion is purely a formality, if any director objects to a certain section of the report, and this statement does not include a recommendation, so it will not be naturally raised for consideration after the report has been accepted, the director can propose an amendment, that is, to accept the report, but excluding a certain part, the so-called certain part being the part that the director objects to. Once the motion (please accept the report) is passed, the recommendations in the report are submitted by the chairman in order and the ones that are adopted will be the resolutions of the Board of Directors. The chairman of the committee can make a statement to the Board of Directors on any recommendation in the report and ask for it to be passed, but even if the chairman does not do so, once the numbers of the report sections including each recommendation are submitted by the chairman or the chief administrator of the Municipal Council, it will be considered that the recommendation has been moved by the chairman for approval. However, if the chairman states in advance that he does not agree with the recommendation, then the recommendation should be moved for approval by other members of the committee. If so, the various recommendations can be debated one by one, just like an ordinary proposal, and an amendment can be proposed. This amendment mostly comes from the process of moving, ordering that the events recommended be resubmitted to the committee for consideration, and informing the committee of the points that the Board of Directors believes need to be reconsidered before a final decision is made.

38. Based on what I have observed, the procedure currently used by the Municipal Council Board of Directors to dispose of matters submitted by various committees is to accept in general terms everything discussed by the committee as recorded in the minutes of the previous committee meeting. The more important parts of the minutes are sometimes read out, and the major events are verbally explained by the chairman of the committee. The committee's resolutions are also explained by the chairman of the committee if they seem to need further explanation. However, each item recorded in the committee's meeting minutes is not submitted to the Board of Directors separately. If the directors have any questions about certain matters, they must wait until the chairman of the committee has finished explaining everything recorded in the minutes before they can raise them.

Submitting the various events recorded in the sections of the report that have been marked with numbers separately, referring to the chairman of the committee for further explanation when necessary, and debating them, and immediately deciding on the first event before the second event is submitted, I believe that this method can usually prove to be far more convenient than the current procedure, and the minds of the directors can be less laborious than at present, because according to the current procedure, after explaining the matters recorded in the latter part of the committee meeting minutes, it may be necessary to return to discuss the matters recorded in the previous part. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Essay

Headlong Down a Dead End vs. (Seeking Another Path) 177

— Zeng Yu

(1) Foreign Aggression. More than a year has passed in the blink of an eye since the September 18th Incident last year. The enemy has been advancing steadily, starting with seizing our land, then organizing a puppet regime, and recognizing a puppet state. Looking back at our government and people, they have been running around and appealing. Today, they send a telegram to the League of Nations to maintain world peace, and tomorrow, they appeal to the great powers to uphold the Nine-Power Treaty. The enemy has seized our customs duties, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issues a protest. The enemy then attacks Rehe, and the government issues a telegram. But no matter how many times the protests are issued, and no matter how many telegrams are sent every day, what has been their effect over the past year? Everyone knows that it is equal to zero.

(2) Internal Warfare. At this time of such severe national crisis, the domestic warlords are staging their best performances. In the past, there were the two Chens in Guangdong, and now there are Han and Liu in Shandong, and the two Lius in Sichuan. Due to the frequent occurrence of internal warfare, a civil organization called the Anti-War Grand Alliance has emerged, and they send telegrams to these warlords (The national crisis is urgent, hoping for unified unity), (Another telegram is issued), (Those who are willing to be the first to use force will be abandoned by the people). But regardless of your national crisis or your being abandoned by the people, their good shows are being performed with great vigor, so the more telegrams are sent, the more vigorously they perform. In the end, its effect is also equal to zero.

Using the above two events as proof, it can be known that Chinese people are doing things in a way that is always (heading down a dead end). But the facts have already told you that (heading down a dead end) is useless and will not solve all your difficulties. So now there are many people loudly calling for (seeking another path). Speaking of (seeking another path), this may not be a good way to remedy the situation, but whether this other (path) can be found, and what its effect will be after it is found, is another question. Some people say that because (another path) cannot be found, it can only be (heading down a dead end). Because it can only be (heading down a dead end), there is no hope of resolving China's (foreign aggression) and (internal warfare) forever. When I heard this sentence, I felt that it made sense, but after thinking carefully, I want to ask China, which is organized by such a large population of 400 million people!

Is it really impossible to find another path?

Is it really going to be like this forever (heading down a dead end)?

Science

A Simple Method for Making Furs 179

— Tianlong

Indeed, we are powerless to process furs such as gray squirrel and fox fur, and can only sigh with envy. However, we can process ordinary sheep, dog, cat, rat, and yellow weasel furs anytime, anywhere, and their cost is very low, so why not do it? Now, I will write down the simple method below:

First, soak the raw or dry fur with hair in water (use cold water mixed with 0.1% caustic soda and carbolic acid) to restore it to its original state. Then, place it on a sloping wooden board and use a pure knife to scrape off the unnecessary parts on the flesh side (the knife edge should be perpendicular to the flesh side when scraping, and the thickness should be even). Then, use an iron comb to remove the old hair from the fur side. Then, apply red clay on the flesh side and expose it to the sun to allow the fat in the fur to be completely absorbed into the red clay. Then, use a wooden stick to knock off the clay and wash it clean with water. Then, you can start the tanning process. The tanning of fur is very simple. Just throw the fur, which has been prepared as described above, into various suitable tanning liquors (note) for immersion. The ordinary immersion time is about one or two days, but it must be fully stirred and reversed several times. After the tanning liquor is completely absorbed, it can be taken out to dry and embellished to become a bright and soft fur.

(Note) There are many types of fur tanning liquors, which can be roughly divided into: (1) using leather alum, salt, and rice flour; (2) using alum and salt; (3) using salt and oils; (4) using chrome salts; (5) using tannin or Fornaine. There are also those who mix several solutions for tanning. In short, it depends on the type of original fur. For skins like sheep, cats, and yellow weasels mentioned above, it is sufficient to use the first method of leather alum, salt, and rice flour, or the second method of alum and salt.

Society Improvement Discussion Group

Discussion on the Issue of Preserving or Abolishing Ancestral Halls 180

— Wenbing

This column previously published an article by Mr. Wang Shibeng (Discussion on Improving the Management of Ancestral Halls). The author's intention is to improve the management of ancestral halls, which naturally acknowledges that they have a need to exist. This is originally each person's opinion and proposition. I only wish to offer my other opinion for public reference.

I do not agree with the management improvement of ancestral halls, and especially do not agree with the existence of ancestral halls. My major premise is: fundamentally abolish them. The reasons are as follows.

In terms of today's era trend, the existence of feudal remnants is no longer allowed, but it is ubiquitous in Chinese society. The ancestral hall of the clan is one of the most powerful forms of feudalism. In addition to the concept of home, Chinese people also have the clan. Therefore, the clan organization is the most sound, and the authority is also very large. The clan head of each clan can simply be said to be a local emperor. There are certainly good local emperors, but there are always more bad ones. In society, they often use the power of the clan to act arbitrarily and influence all matters, large and small. For example, if two families, A and B, are involved in a lawsuit, and family A is originally in the wrong, the clan head and others often forcibly seize the upper hand in order to maintain the reputation of their clan. Therefore, they do not hesitate to pawn ancestral property and bribe and collude with the government at all costs, making a very ordinary trivial matter unable to rest, wasting much energy and money, and also causing the emotions of both parties to deteriorate, regarding each other as enemies. Fights between clans often occur in various parts of Guangdong, often resulting in numerous casualties and generations of feuds. In the eyes of ordinary people, they still think it is to bring honor to the clan, and it is glorious even in death. Clan public funds are always encroached upon and swallowed by a few powerful people over time, or they are used as an excuse for sacrifices to hold grand banquets, eat and drink heavily, wasting social resources. In the past, if someone in the clan passed the imperial examinations, they would definitely hang some plaques. Now, graduates of schools also still play this trick. The most is that

Page 18

when descendants work as officials outside, scraping the fat off the people, they return to their clan in glory, repair the ancestral hall, and hang plaques. In addition, if the clan head has a long life, there are even more tricks, such as hanging plaques and putting on operas. In short, with the existence of ancestral halls, we only see them heading towards vanity and consumption everywhere, and there is no benefit to speak of.

They are indifferent to the major national affairs outside the clan. For example, I have never heard of any clan generously donating to the Northeast Volunteer Army, and I have also never heard of any giant clan donating how much to the ancient water disaster last year. When encountering national affairs, they hold on to the principle of (each person sweeps the snow in front of their own door) and clutch their money bags, unwilling to let go.

Based on the above, it is sufficient to abolish ancestral halls. Moreover, today's society simply does not allow the existence of such feudal organizations. In today's harsh environment where we are pressed by strong neighbors, we should originally only have national concepts and the concept of all mankind. Undoubtedly, this narrow family concept and family organization should be abolished.

What to do after abolishing them? I can also offer some suggestions:

The buildings of ancestral halls occupy a large area. If they are used as factories or schools, they are all good places. Or they can be used as orphanages, civilian residences, or public hospitals. It all depends on the local social environment. If they are near cities, it is of course appropriate to run factories, orphanages, and hospitals. If they are in rural areas, it is better to use them as small school buildings or public libraries.

All public properties should also be used to run the above-mentioned undertakings, and absolutely no one or two powerful clan heads should be allowed to swallow them privately. However, this method will be difficult to achieve if it is only promoted verbally. The government must issue an order to force implementation. Then, those with rigid minds will naturally have to (hold their right heads in their mouths and worship the sky) and there will be no possibility of opposition.

Finally, I want to say: today's Chinese society is truly extremely unprogressive. We only see conservatism everywhere, and only see bad conservatism. We are unwilling to earnestly innovate, so the society and the country are not only unable to catch up with the world trend, but are also becoming increasingly backward. We urgently need to broaden our horizons, focus on the transcendence of the nation and the country, and the co-existence and co-prosperity of mankind, and no longer allow ourselves to inherit traditions and fix our eyes on the family.

Postscript: I had just finished drafting this article when I suddenly received a letter from a friend in Changsha, saying that his family was being bullied and their ancestral property was being encroached upon by a neighboring family, and they are now in litigation, asking me to invite friends to forcefully issue public votes. Because it is related to this article, I have attached it as a note.

A Test of Love 181

— Hongshui

Since Miss Qian, a typist, was newly hired at the Changyun Company, the huge office felt much more lively. Mr. Yuan Hao, who had always been taciturn and looked stern, now often floated with a smile and chatted with Miss Qian. As for Mr. Ding, who has always been known as the (young master), he always keeps his hair smooth, his trouser creases straight, and Mr. Hong, the accountant's loud and endless voice, goes without saying.

In short, everything has lost its normality since Miss Qian came and added a touch of red to the myriad greens.

Every morning, when Miss Qian's beautiful figure is about to catch the eye of every colleague, everyone will ask this shy Miss Qian good morning in a gentle and kind tone. Her fluffy hair brushed her forehead, good delicate peach cheeks, blue eyes, bright red lips, her face applied with a thin layer of fragrant powder, wearing a bright and dazzling dress, and even wearing rings and watches with precious light and pearl energy. Her decoration in this office is just like that (shadow enamel) vase on the table!

Jing, Wen, and Qin live in Dormitory No. 6. One month later, under the moonlight one night, Jing suddenly talked about it with great interest.

(Mr. Ding and Miss Qian seem to have something going on?)

(Oh?) Qin straightened her ears and stretched her neck, expressing extreme welcome to the following.

(That's right, I have noticed this too.) Wen also said as if he had caught iron evidence about their (sexual problem).

(Why?) At this time, Qin had put down a book about the Camellia Girl that she was engrossed in and raised her head.

(Qin, are you still pretending? They often go in and out of parks, movie theaters, and dance halls in pairs. Don't you know or have you not noticed?) Jing said.

(That's right! This is absolutely true.) Wen chimed in.

(Is this worth making a fuss about in this era of open social interaction?)

(Then are you saying that there is nothing wrong with them? Okay! Let me and Wen think of a good plan to test the degree of their love for you to see!) Jing said, looking up at the eyeballs and frowning, as if thinking deeply about something.

The next day. It was Saturday afternoon. Mr. Ding suddenly received a letter in which Miss Qian asked him to watch a movie at the Carlton at 3 pm on Sunday? At the same time, Miss Qian also received a letter in which Mr. Ding invited her to talk at Zhao Feng Park at 9 am on Sunday? The wording of the two letters was very simple, and each recipient only glanced at them hastily, but they could all get a kind of pleasure.

Miss Qian did indeed arrive at the park early in the morning. She looked around and around until after eleven o'clock. Not only did she not see Mr. Ding's shadow, but she also inadvertently ran into Jing, Wen, and Qin's friends who she hated. She was really embarrassed to the extreme!

Mr. Ding, who had been standing in front of the Carlton door for a long time, had already bought two flower floor show tickets and held them in his hands, almost sweating. He watched a pair of beautiful people fill the seats one after another. The pleasant music also stopped, and the movie started. However, the beauty who wrote the letter inviting him to watch the movie丨Miss Qian's arrival was not seen. At this moment, he was so anxious and resentful that he could not add to it, but he still had to meet a group of smiling brothers, naturally the old Jings, the inventors of the love test in Dormitory No. 6!

Matching Eight Characters 182

— Shizi

(A Jin, I told you to invite the master, did you invite him?)

Mrs. Wang called A Jin to invite Mr. Zhang, the fortune teller of XX Road, to come and match the marriage for the second young master after dinner. (Madam! The master has been invited. He is waiting in the hall now. Please go out to talk to him.) A Jin replied.

(Madam, you are out. How have you been?) Mr. Zhang sat in the hall and saw Mrs. Wang coming out from inside at a glance, and immediately stood up from the chair and greeted her with a smile.

(Please sit down, Mr. Zhang! I invited you here today not for anything else, but because my second young master is now seventeen years old, and it is time to find a match. I am thankful that several relatives and friends think highly of him, and many wedding invitations have been sent from all directions. I think marriage is a major matter and should not be taken lightly. Whether the couple will get along well in the future depends on whether the eight characters are chosen appropriately now. If one is careless and mismatches the conflicting eight characters, then one's happiness will be completely buried. So I am asking you to come today to match these eight characters and choose a compatible one so that I can proceed with the engagement.) After Madam finished speaking, she took out a roll of red paper from her pocket and handed it to Mr. Zhang to assess and match.

Mr. Zhang saw a stack of eight characters, looking at this one and looking at that one, muttering ghosts and spirits in his mouth, and turning the zodiac signs in his hands, and slowly said; (Madam, please listen quietly! This eight character of the Jin surname is not good to use because there are two layers of Seven Killings, the life is too hard, and the Li surname is not good to use either, because there is an Injury Officer in the fate. The book says that if a man has a Yang Blade, he must remarry, and if a woman has an Injury Officer, she will definitely overcome her husband. Therefore, although I heard that Miss Li is virtuous and knowledgeable, this injury officer is a big problem and must not be used.)

(Sir! Then how about one of the Chen surnames? I heard that this young lady is also very gentle and capable. If the fate is good to use, that would be the best.)

Mr. Zhang hurriedly picked out the Chen surname's eight characters and carefully looked at it, and then moved his five fingers east and west for a while to calculate, shaking his head and saying; (Madam, this eight character is even worse. There is a Yin Yang Cross in the fate, which means overcoming the in-laws.)

(Don't calculate, sir. Burn this eight character. How can you take out the life of a public mother and harm people?) Madam was full of anger at the time, and snatched the eight characters from Mr. Zhang's hand, struck a match, and burned it before saying again; (Although I am already sixty years old this year, I still want to live, so I hate it the most when people take out the eight characters of a public mother. Sir!

Please check other ones.)

Mr. Zhang laughed secretly in his heart, thinking that he had said (offending the mother-in-law) in his mouth and made her old man so anxious, so he pretended to be extremely solemn, and checked the stack of eight characters again, muttering in his mouth again;

(This one is guilty of looking forward to being a widow, it is not good to use, that one has many seals in the four pillars, and will be red-haired and sleepless in the future, it is not good to use either.) Later, he discovered a Hong surname, who had a relative relationship with himself, and then said; (Okay, okay, this eight character is born on the day of longevity, the official star is revealed, and the wealth and seals are all complete, named San Bao, which can be predicted to be prosperous for the husband and benefit the children. It is truly a life of wealth and honor, and there is nothing better.)

When Mrs. Wang heard that the Hong surname's eight characters were so good, she was overjoyed and smiled and nodded, saying; (Okay, I am very satisfied with such a good eight character. This is also the blessing of the second son. Now I don't need to check anything else. I am determined to use this one, sir, thank you for your trouble.)

Even Stronger Than a Big Sale 183

— Wenbing

丨Description in a Lecture on National Economics丨

After eating a late breakfast at nine o'clock, I had just picked up the pen and wanted to write something deceptive丨writing, when Guan Ren suddenly came in excitedly. He stepped over the threshold and said the first sentence;

(I'm here to invite you to buy cheap goods. XX Company is still having a big sale, buy one get one free, and free gifts!)

(Why are you so flustered, speak slowly丨Please sit down!) I stood up and shook hands with him tightly, and continued to say;

(There are so many tricks in Shanghai. Various shops have at least four fun times a year. What sales, price cuts, cheap sales, big auctions, and the words spring, summer, autumn, and winter are crowned according to the different seasons, with flowery trimmings, mouths singing and shouting, and drums and music playing. In addition, there are several anniversaries and Dragon Boat Festival and Mid-Autumn Festival, which are crowned with the words (special) big sale. People who come to Shanghai for the first time often fully believe that things they usually need should be bought at this time.

In fact, to be honest, once the goods are in the hands of merchants, will we really enjoy cheap goods? At most, we can slightly leak a little profit from the big sale tricks of earning a few less. When everyone goes to buy, the goods are sold even more, and the merchants will become even richer. Moreover, if you are not careful, you will be unexpectedly fooled. Therefore, many people who are used to living in Shanghai do not regard big sales as a great opportunity.)

(Then, according to you, we don't need to go to XX Company today!) Guan Ren was a little disappointed, supporting the back of his head with both hands, and lying half-inclined on my wooden bed.

(Yes, I don't agree with going! 丨丨It's really hard to say myself, not long ago, I was fooled once, and I bought a pair of overshoes for four coppers, which was considered cheap, but when I brought them back, I only wore them twice, and there were two copper-sized holes in the bottom. Guan Ren, think about it, is it cheap or not?)

Guan Ren was completely convinced by me.

(That's good, saving a few dollars, life next month will be more secure!)

(That's right! Speaking of big sales, I can also tell you something worth studying. Fukuda Tokuzo said in a lecture on national economics ····· In one year, the price of ginseng in Shanghai and other markets in China plummeted ····· So, not knowing on whose idea, a lot of the precious ginseng was burned at the Incheon pier ····· This matter, from the point of view of (things), is very unreasonable, because it is very effective to use this thing as medicine. Now, this useful thing is burned without hesitation. People who don't know it will definitely think it is a waste and uneconomical, but in fact it is very economical. How can I say that? Because the people who bought ginseng immediately came to buy it when they heard about the burning of ginseng at the Incheon pier, so in less than a few days, the ginseng market in Shanghai recovered, and the remaining ginseng was sold at a very high price. In this way, selling the burned ginseng at a high price is more profitable than selling all the ginseng at a low price.

There are many people in the world who want to eat ginseng but cannot get ginseng to eat. At this time, many ready-made ginsengs are burned. This is called being in line with the way of economics. Studying this kind of economics is called national economics.

Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court 185

Criminal Judgment in the case of Chen Minzhang et al. endangering the Republic of China (Main Text) Chen Minzhang and Fang Jie jointly propagandized doctrines incompatible with the Three Principles of the People for the purpose of endangering the Republic of China, each sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be used to offset the imprisonment, with two days offsetting one day of imprisonment. ▲ The case of Ni Zhiyao suspected of smoking opium (Main Text) The original judgment regarding the guilt and punishment of Ni Zhiyao is revoked. Ni Zhiyao is innocent. ▲ The case of Xiao Qiming involving Cheng Yuqing's fraud and breach of trust (Main Text) The appeal is dismissed. ▲ The case of the Shanghai Municipal Council involving the Russian Yabalingk's fraud (Main Text) The original judgment is revoked and remanded to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court for a new trial. ▲ The case of Wu Fushou endangering public morals (Main Text) The original judgment regarding Wu Fushou's crime of enticing prostitution, the execution of punishment, and offsetting punishment are all revoked. Wu Fushou jointly enticed a woman under the age of sixteen to commit adultery with others and was sentenced to one year of imprisonment. Together with the punishment for the crime of hindering freedom in the original judgment, one year of imprisonment is executed. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be used to offset the imprisonment, with two days offsetting one day of imprisonment. The rest of the appeal is dismissed. ▲ The case of Cen Xiquan endangering the Republic of China (Main Text) Cen Xiquan was fined two hundred yuan for continuously publishing publications intended to subvert the National Government. If the fine is not paid in full, it will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be used to offset the fine, with one day offsetting two yuan. The People's Daily three-day publication of 650 copies is confiscated. ▲ The case of Zhou Huaifa et al. endangering public morals (Main Text) The original judgment regarding the guilt and punishment of Zhou Huaifa, Zhou Hongyuan, and Chen Fuying is revoked. Zhou Hongyuan and Chen Fuying jointly lured a woman under the age of twenty away from a person who has close kinship for the purpose of making profits, each sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be used to offset the imprisonment, with two days offsetting one day of imprisonment. Zhou Huaifa is innocent.

Public Announcement: Regarding the announcement of the case of Wu Zhushi vs. Cao Xiaomei et al. for inheritance disputes, the Jiangsu Shanghai Local Court has ruled that the plaintiff has the right to manage the shares of 2,000 yuan in the Xifei Flower Shop and 500 yuan in the Mingji Flower Shop invested by Wu Wufu. Cao Xiaomei shall hand over the capital contract of Wu Wufu's Mingji Flower Shop shares to the plaintiff for safekeeping. The contract signed between Cao Xiaomei, Zhu Fugeng, and Zhou Xisheng regarding the joint establishment of the Xifei Flower Shop shall be deemed invalid. The litigation costs in this case shall be borne by Cao Xiaomei. The court is requested to assist in execution. Upon the court detaining Cao Xiaomei, she was strictly ordered to hand over the contracts as stated in the judgment, but Cao Xiaomei refused to do so. Therefore, according to Article 92 of the Revised Rules of Civil Procedure Execution, this announcement is made for public knowledge. After this announcement, the contract for 500 yuan in shares of Wu Wufu's Mingji Flower Shop held by Cao Xiaomei is declared invalid. This announcement is hereby made. (The above is from October 27th)
